<Content>Great Value in Waikiki We stayed 16 nights in the Diamond Tower-we booked the ocean view hotel room-the room was small and clean with an outstanding ocean view between the hotels in front of us-We have stayed here before in the Pali Tower Kitchenette Room-The Diamond Tower is less noisy and will definately stay here again-This hotel to me is such a bargain for those who want a simple room to sleep in-if you are fussy and want alot of amenities this hotel is not for you. I used to be a travel agent and after comparing many hotels at varying prices I really think the Castle Ocean Resort is a huge bargain. Our room only had a refridgerator so if you want more I would suggest staying in the Pali Tower.It is a3-5 minute walk to Waikiki Beach-on the side by the Zoo-there is an enclosed area that is great for families with children-Hope this helps-I know there are some bad reviews for this hotel but you'll get none from me-Aloha

<Author>LesterB
<Content>Three rooms over the weekend We were in Honolulu for a wedding this weekend. We had 3 rooms booked at the Ocean Resort for $89 so we weren't expecting luxury. Room #1 was sort of like a shanty, twin bedded, it looked like a dorm. Room #2 was small, one queen bed, nice ocean views though not full-on as the Marriott is in the way. Room #3--OMIGOD, our friends arrived late in the day, all the rooms were full, and they got upgraded to a penthouse. It was ENORMOUS, maybe 1100 square feet---2 baths, dining room table for 6, 2 balconies, 2 giant couches and TV in living room, HUGE king size bedded separate bedroom, kitchenette. They good naturedly lorded this $89 extravaganza over us but were magnanimous in inviting us to loll in their palatial digs! It was a real treat.Overall this hotel is kind of shabby though the location is great. Parking is by valet only and can take some time to retrieve car. 2 out of 3 elevators were broken so there were some long lines which caused grumbling.

<Author>skattieSitka
<Content>Quiet at the Ocean Resort Hotel What I really liked about the Ocean Resort Hotel, was that I could not hear my neighbors. The walls must really be thick, it was great. It is very conveniently located to the beach. It has two pools, a restaurant in the lobby, although I did not use the restaurant. We stayed on the 11th floor, had a kitchenette and balcony. The kitchenette has a coffee machine, microwave, small fridge, a little hotplate, and crockery and cutlery. We did not need anything more. A little snafu with my reservation when I arrived, but the front desk personnel took care of it very quickly. A very nice stay for a very reasonable price. The tub and basin was a little scratched and old, the carpets were a little dirty, housekeeping was not perfect, but still worth it. No luxury, but I got what I paid for.

<Author>ElFeliz
<Content>Very Nice for the Price I booked this hotel through Orbitz- I was apprehensive because I read a number of negative reviews and the rate was quite a bit less than other near-by properties. My daughter's hotel, Hotel Renew, was a few doors away, and because she was being married, I wanted to be close before the wedding, but not intrusive.The hotel is just what the doctor ordered- steps away from the whole Waikiki experience, clean and secure, this place is a hidden gem.The hotel staff, for the most part, was friendly and accommodating. In fact, upon check-in, I was informed that a regular bed, which I had booked, would be uncomfortable for me, as I am a big guy. I was up-graded to a queen sized bed-room, free. I had a spectacular view of the city of Honolulu from the 10th floor. The hotel provides valet parking only, I simply parked on the street each night, with no problems. The hotel has an activity desk where you can book tours and other activities. The biggest advantage, is the hotel is a block away from Waikiki Beach.The room was clean and tidy with a mini-fridge. An ABC store (think: upscale 7-11) is a few doors away should you want to stock your fridge with beverages and snacks Though a bit worn, though not seedy, the hotel has a great reputation with the local tour operators. The room was comfortable with a small balcony which I was able to appreciate in the evenings, though the balcony chairs were a bit uncomfortable for long stretches of sitting. No in-room internet access, though the hotel has a cyber-type cafe on the first floor lobby. If you are in need of an iron or need to do your laundry, you will have to go down to the 2nd floor laundry area to do these things. The hotel is family friendly so expect to run into kids, though unlike some of the other area hotels, it does become quiet during the night. The hotel is busy early and then quiets down a bit just before noon. Over-all, I found the hotel a very nice experience. My flight to the mainland did not leave until 10pm - the hotel staff was gracious enough to lock away my luggage until I retrieved it for the trip to the airport later that evening.ONE WARNING: Stay away from hotel dining room- the staff was rude, arrogant, obnoxious and down right dishonest. I visited once and that was enough for me. I ordered a side of Garlic Fries, though not listed on the menu, regular Fries were listed on the menu with a side of Garlic bread for 4.50- the waiter returned with fries that were lightly covered with garlic powder- for 7.50- when I pointed out the discrepancy in the price, the waiter, who was also the bartender and the cashier, declared the fries were covered in fresh garlic and that he observed the chef apply the fresh garlic. This was such a blatant lie that I could hardly contain my laughter. They refused to accept American Express and were very nasty and impolite about it. To make matters worse, the food was terribly bland and obviously processed and/or frozen. With so many other dining choices nearby, avoid this place with purpose and intention, but enjoy the hotel- as it is a great place for the price- all the tour buses stop there and I will be returning. Definitely worth a stay and a try!  
<Date>Jul 25, 2008

We paid $165 per room and it was TOTALLY NOT WORTH THE MONEY!!!! This is a 1 or MAYBE 2 star hotel. The location was the only bonus to this hotel. It was only a couple blocks from Waikiki beach.

<Author>Leota1313
<Content>Above-average budget accomodations We stayed at the Ocean Resort in October of 2006. We found it to be more than adequate. The rooms were clean and a decent size. The location was very good. The beach at the end of the street is a sort of swimming lagoon. It's not a very good beach, but you can walk 3 minutes to where it's better. And really, Waikiki is probably the worst beach on Oahu. If you hang out only at Waikiki, you're really missing out! There are plenty of restaurants and shops in walking distance of the hotel. There's a small restaurant and bar in the lobby, but they aren't really worth it unless you're desperate; you can easily walk to something better in 5 minutes. Of note, we were in Oahu when the 6.7 earthquake in Hawaii occurred. The power went out on the entire island for almost a whole day. The staff at the hotel were very accommodating. They had a radio and provided the guests with updates on the situation. Our room was still cleaned that day, even though the power was out.The only issue we had was upon check-in: we arrived about an hour before we could check in. They didn't even check if any rooms were ready; they just told us to come back at 2pm. So we went out for a while, came back at 2pm. They first thing the employee at the desk did was to check the clock to be sure it was after 2pm. This seemed a little rude. I mean, at least PRETEND that we can't check in because they are cleaning the rooms or something, not because it's not exactly 2pm. All in all, the Ocean Resort is small and has no frills, but if you're looking for a good deal and a good location, it more than fits the bill.

<Content>Great location / Dirty room My family of 4 stayed here in April of 08. I had read some of the reviews on tripadvisor but thought since we are not particularly picky people it would be fine. Unfortunatly, the place was just to much to handle. While I will agree with others that the location is great, and the rooms are big I don鈥檛 think I would stay here again because the rooms were dirty. I would wager that this was a top notch hotel when it was built sometime I would guess in the 60s, but it hasn鈥檛 been updated at all. I would venture to guess that it hasn鈥檛 be thoroughly cleaned since then either. The carpets are filthy and there was mildew in the bathroom and shower. The location is an easy walk to the ponds on Waikiki. We were on the 3rd floor non ocean view. We did enjoy ourselves despite the hotel.

<Author>SEmigh
<Content>LARGE room, great location! We stayed for one night (Saturday) prior to flying home. We had four adults in our group, and received a room with a lanai viewing Diamond Head, I think on the 12th floor. The room had two double beds and a single bed, and was not crowded. Also had a small kitchenette. Medium sized but adequate TV. The air conditioner worked very well. Didn't notice any street noise. As other reviews mention, this room was very large...much larger than rooms in newer hotels for a comparable price. While it's a little worn around the edges and older, it's clean and plenty of towels are provided in the bathroom. The shower and toilet are in a separate area from the bathroom sink. Must pay for parking, and your car is parked for you. Had a fine breakfast in the restaurant, which is located in the open air lobby. The desk service was very competent and courteous. Located very close to the beach, on the scenic end of Waikiki. Loved it!

<Author>Clown_Guy
<Content>Great Location - Budget Accomodations We stayed at Ocean Resort for two separate nights during our current trip to Hawaii. This is the second time we stayed at the Ocean Resort. The first time was four years ago as part of the Your Man Tours travel itinerary. This time we stayed the day we flew into and the night we flew out of Oahu. We spent the rest of the time on the North Shore. We did not rent a car while we stayed here. We rented the car only when we left for the North Shore as we knew parking was a problem here. We took the airport shuttle to get here and a taxi when we left. We arrived at the Hotel prior to the stated check in time. The person we dealt with at the front desk was very professional and allowed us to check in early (both times). We had booked the lowest level room both times and definitely got it. The room was very nice in all respects, but the view. There was none! Our view was of an apartment building next door. The first time we stayed, we had an obstructed view of the ocean. I don鈥檛 think I would pay more for the view as we were always on the go. We used the room for sleeping and washing up and it was excellent for that. The room was clean, the bed comfortable and the shower hot. We did eat breakfast one morning at the hotel and it was very good. I would highly recommend the Macadamia Nut Pancakes. The second morning we had to leave early to get to the airport. The person at the front desk helped us out to get a taxi. We needed a mini van style taxi as we he had a lot of luggage (most of our trip was camping). He called a taxi company and got us a cab in the time frame we required. As noted in other reviews, the location is excellent on a quieter street. I would have no problem staying here again if we ever come to Waikiki again.

<Author>JR26385
<Content>People Need To Be Realistic Stayed at the Ocean Resort many, many times beginning in 2003. I've seen most of the things pointed out in the negative posts: few ants, peeling wallpaper, old carpets, .... but this is not typical. The only time I complained (got 2 small beds) I was able to move the next morning.People need to be realistic. The hotel is priced at the low end of the hotels, right above the real rat traps. If you're on your honeymoon, or your trip of a lifetime, or will spend lots of time in the room then don't pay next to nothing and expect the Ritz.The location is excellent. Its 1.5 blocks from the beach and is on the quieter side of Waikiki. Its about 10 minutes from leaving your hotel room until you're spreading the towel on the beach. Its near the zoo, aquarium, and Kapiolani park and there are plenty of places for short, moderate, and very long walks/runs. I've done the ~7 mile round trip hike from hotel to the top of Diamond Head and back a few times. Its also 50 yards from a The Bus stop, and a short walk to fastfood, Chili's, very good Korean/Chinese take out, good steak house, grocery store, lots of ABC stores, and a 15 minute walk to the center of Waikiki and much more.The rooms are generally clean and a little worn but are cleaned nicely on a daily basis. I've found the front desk to be above average for this class of hotel.

<Author>DWGPND
<Content>The only thing this hotel has going for it is its location Great location at the end of Waikiki. Less than five minute walk to the beach. The hotel is old and in need of a serious upgrade. The electrical wiring in our tower couldn't even support the use of an iron. Clothes must be ironed on the 2nd floor. This is great if you're on the 2nd floor. The rooms we're outdated and the views non-existent. The lobby was dirty and the staff not the friendliest. Don't bother asking for anything other than what's in your room (extra glasses, towels, sheets, etc). What you see is all you get. Overall, it's a decent place to hang your hat while you're at the beach and not expecting the higher-end amenities of the neighboring resorts. It's a budget hotel with zero frills.

<Author>Captronnz
<Content>I Hope They Read Their Own Reviews Here First let me say the hotel was as expected for the reasonable price paid, and as reviewed elsewhere here however; a few 鈥榮mall鈥?improvements would have made the stay so MUCH better, and if these things were done, I would not hesitate to go back there. The staff were mostly helpful, checking and out was fast  friendly and most hall staff were excellent. The room was dated but clean and tidy, and as we chose the low cost senior package, it was not very large. Location is quite decent with easy bus access.The three main areas that would have made our stay so much better are:Air Conditioner. As you can imaginer, Hawaii is hot and muggy and the A/C plays a big part in the day-to-day enjoyment. We had to work a few days in the room and it was dreadful, the nights were similar for this device. It was not a central unit, but rather the old motel window mounted units, with the associated noise and vibration, not to mention falling apart in places. Hot nights were draughty and noisy when running even on low. We resorted to covering up the front partly with paper to reduce the draught, and waking up to turn off an on so we could sleep right. Answer: Either an expensive upgraded central ducted system with individual controls. In fact I鈥檓 not an advocate of these sorts of A/C systems as they can carry germs etc, so the easy answer is to install low cost heat pump, with the compressor outside, possibly on the Ext wall away from the deck, and the low volume quite evaporator inside. These are common everywhere these day and the new Freon 410a units are super-quiet and super efficient meaning they would pay for themselves over time.Bathroom: While this room was clean, the maintenance was appalling, with loose controls, poor shower heat control and plugged showerhead. Overall other than this it was OK.Internet: Low cost in room Internet was just not available. We did eventually get access through a wireless provider off site. Not all rooms can face the required direction. Cost was $25 per week, and worked well while we were there. This is such an easy thing to fix, and we end up spending days sorting out access.Comments about the dining room are true with Breakfast (Once) being OK, but as there are other places nearby, this was not an issue.CheersFrom Auckland NZ

<Author>Msagro
<Content>We were rather surprised! I must say that after reading all the reviews, my husband and I were quite surprised. We thought we would be walking into a dump! The staff was pleasant and gave us the opportunity to look at a standard room and an upgraded room before checking in. We elected to stay in the standard room (as we were rarely there) so we could spend the $30 a night to upgrade on other things. Our room was neat and clean, the bed was confortable and our maid was always so cheerful that we tipped her a little something everyday. Our only negative with the room was the extremely noisy air conditioner. But once we put the earplugs in at night (which I had brought because my hubby snores) we were good to go. One evening the weather was stormy and little did we know but the power went out while we were sleeping. This resulted in us not getting our wake-up call the next morning for a tour we had paid to go on. The hotel manager was very apologetic, offered to buy us another tour if the tour company wouldn't reschedule us (which they did) and bought us breakfast (which wasn't that bad - it was our only meal there). It is very close to the beach and the ABC store and thank goodness for the tip on parking at the parking garage across the street (The Banyan). All in all, it was a great, cheap trip. Would do it again!

<Author>kmac65
<Content>Wonderful Bargain We spent nine nights here in September, 2007. After reviewing other hotels for price and location, we chose the Ocean Resort and had a penthouse (The Oahu) in the Pali Tower facing the ocean. With a senior rate this was very affordable -- especially for Waikiki Beach! The room was large; the ocean view was great. The balcony facing the ocean was small but held two chairs and a table and was perfect for sunset watching. The refrigerator was very tiny but held our water and some snacks. No stove/oven but only a hot plate. We were on vacation and weren't going to cook meals so that didn't matter to us. I had read many of the previous negative reviews. I found none of the negatives present on our stay. The bathroom and entire suite were clean with fresh towels every day. The room was ready upon our arrival and was always cleaned early while we were out. We never had more than a minute wait for an elevator coming or going. The front desk staff was helpful and the concierge helped us with one driving trip. The location of the Ocean Resort is about a two-block (very short blocks) walk to the ocean. It's located at the Diamond Head end of Waikiki Beach and not as frantic as further down the beach. The zoo is right around the corner. Several restaurants and snack shops were close. I had heard the parking was expensive and only valet. That's true. But self-parking at the Banyan Hotel across the street was half the price with easy in and out any time. We would definitely stay at the Ocean Resort again.

<Author>dragonman64
<Content>Old and tired but still dependable True, this place has seen better days. The whole lobby reeks of an outdated 80s flair that will never go unnoticed to the eagle-eyed hotel reviewer. The only restaurant-cum-bar lounge can really look miserable (except during breakfast time when large tour groups troop for their first meal of the day) when you're only one of a few dining guests. The two elevators leading to the Pali Tower are slow and - while waiting - you can either play a guessing game of which one of the two units would open first or check out the items displayed on the gift shop window before one of the units would open. Bell service is hit-or-miss, especially if you arrive with a busload of tourists.Nevertheless, I commend Ocean Resort Hotel for having one of the better locations in the quieter part of the Waikiki area. The walking distance to the beach itself is a breeze, while bus and trolley stops are just a kitty corner away. Additionally, the rooms (read: studios) in the Pali Tower are very spacious, with small handy kitchenettes where you can store or reheat food in a jiffy. Cleanliness is average at best, but I would like to point out that the attentiveness of housekeeping to the guests' needs is worth citing. And in the land of ABC stores, one branch is comfortably nearby.All in all, I would not hesitate in recommending this property if you're on a tight budget. Don't expect too much and you'll end up appreciating your stay. Despite the shortcomings on some areas, the bottomline is they still deliver.

<Author>DanGatineau
<Content>Great place to stay Stayed at the Ocean Resort Hotel in Waikiki for 10 days. It was very well situated, one block from Waikiki beach, the restaurants and shops. You can shop 'til you drop. At the marketplace, you can bargain but not in the stores. The hotel room was clean, had a partial ocean view on the 10th floor and would stay there again. There were Internet stations near the lobby but had access to free Internet (wireless) in the room which was great. We ate breakfast twice at the hotel's restaurant and were satisfied. Most of the time, we ate breakfast in the room, sometimes dinner when we had a late lunch, an ABC store was close so we could buy what we needed, cereal, milk etc. There was a small refrigerator in the room which was very useful. The temperature was ideal, at night you do not have to wear a sweater. During the day, the beach was great, the water was very warm and we loved it. At the ABC store you can buy a parasol for about 16$ which you can use on the beach. You can rent one but it is 20$ for the day so buying one is the best. If you rent a car, there is valet service at the hotel but they charge 15$ a day for parking. One block from the hotel (walking distance a couple of minutes) the opposite direction of the beach, there is parking for 10$ a day so you save 5$ a day. We hope to return there one day.

<Author>nixxi83
<Content>Little romance in this paradise My husband and I had previously been to Hawaii but stayed in a different hotel. We would have returned to that hotel if it weren't for the fact that we kind of overspent on the wedding! So in order to make up for that difference we decided to stay at a hotel that was more in our budget. Through BookIt.com we reserved a room at the Ocean Resort Hotel Waikiki and in the special requests box we wrote that we were on our honeymoon and wanted a room with a queen size bed, which was one of two options for that particular room. We got in late on Wednesday, June 27 and were ready to go to bed after a long layover in LA. After checking in we immediately headed to our room. Despite our specific request we were given a room that had two double beds. We were expected to sleep on seperate beds on our honeymoon! We immediately called the front desk and asked to be changed to another room. They claimed that they were all booked and would not be able to change our room until tomorrow after checkout, and that was only if someone cancelled their reservation because supposedly the hotel was booked. They then suggested that we put the two beds together. So there we were, on our honeymoon, having to rearrange furniture just so we could actually sleep near one another! On top of that the beds were obviously different sizes, one was lower than the other. But the night was not over. Apparently each room in the hotel has it's own WINDOW UNIT! And ours was busted. It made horribly loud noises all night long and I had to turn it off at about 2am because I couldn't sleep with that noise on anymore. Plus that side of the hotel is facing the alley and you can hear car alarms, vehicles, and people talking all throughout the night.The next morning my husband called BookIt and told them about the situation. They then called the hotel and asked what was going on. The front desk immediately said that they would move us to another room that day. So we had to pack up our stuff and turn in the key to the room (218) at 12pm and were not allowed to gain access to our new room until 3pm. That wasn't so bad, afterall there's plenty to do in Waikiki, it was just inconvenient. When we finally returned to the hotel and got into our new room (208) it looked exactly the same except for the queen size bed. Since the room wasn't exactly fresh my husband turned up the AC, about 5 minutes later (and I'm not kidding) the AC unit turned off and wouldn't turn back on. We called the Front Desk and about ten minutes later one of the staff came to check out the problem. It turned out that the unit was messing with the breaker so they had to turn it on to get the unit back on. Before the week was over the unit turned off two more times. The second time it happened it was late and we called the front desk at least two times and no one ever came to the room to respond to our problem. We spent that night, I believe it was Friday the 29th, without any air flowing into the room. Saturday after we were out enjoying the town we made sure to have someone check on the AC. Well, it seems like the person they sent didn't know what they were doing. He said he would check on the breaker and would come back. Well, it seemed that he didn't do anything because the unit never turned on and he never came back!Finally Sunday we actually got someone who knew what to do. For about 30 minutes or so our room look like it was under construction. They had to remove our AC unit and then replaced it with what they claimed to be a new AC unit. And since the door was wide open so the maintenance guy could go in and out of the room with ease the cleaning ladies figured we woudn't care if they decided to work on our room at the same time! I was attempting to take a shower through the whole construction and the one of the cleaning ladies attempted to go into the bathroom while I was in the shower! I had to yell through the door that someone was in the shower and she finally backed off. When I got out of the shower the women were hurrying around me trying to clean up the bathroom and as I was attempting to brush my teeth they were throwing extra soap and shampoo on the counter, they seemed annoyed that I was in the way! I was so mad. All in all we spend 2 1/2 out of 6 nights without any AC running and when we had asked for someone to help us out we were ignored. And if we hadn't called BookIt about our room situation we probably would have been stuck in a room with two double beds our whole honeymoon!I don't believe saving $20 a day was worth dealing with the hassle of staying at Ocean Resort Hotel Waikiki. My suggestion is to stay at a better hotel even if you'll save a few bucks, the hotel was anything but romantic and had no ambience. The bathrooms were tiny, the food in their restaurant was menial and overpriced. I wouldn't want anyone to have the same experience that we had.

<Author>cinogirl
<Content>Huge room, great staff, quiet, excellent value for money We stayed at the Ocean Resort because it was cheap, and because it was across the road from a conference we were attending at the Marriott. In fact we were closer to the conference rooms than people who actually stayed at the Marriott - their rooms were a long way from the conference rooms and they had smaller rooms, their staff weren't as helpful and they paid a lot more for the privilege.We arrived at about 11am and our room was ready (despite the 3pm check-in) and the check-in staff were very friendly and helpful. We had a deluxe kitchenette room and it was HUGE. We had 2 double beds, table and chairs, lots of drawers, and a kitchenette. We were in the Pali Tower on the 14th floor and there was a lanai that you could sit out on (it had a table and 2 chairs) and you could see the ocean on one side (through the buildings), and the mountains on the other. By Australian standards I'd say it was easily a 3 star.The room was very clean and was serviced daily. We saw the housekeeper one morning in the hallway and she greeted us and thanked us for the $2 tip we'd left her; she was lovely.Yes the hotel is old and there is peeling paint and worn carpet but it's not a 5 star hotel and we knew that. I would definitely recommend it if you want to be down that end of town, it's very good value for money. We moved to the Princess Kaualani after the conference, just so we could be in the heart of Waikiki and we preferred the Ocean Resort, except that the PK was a closer location to everything. Having said that, the Ocean Resort isn't far from anything either and it's close to the beach also.We ate in the restaurant at the Ocean Resort and it was okay, nothing special, but cheap enough. Their prime rib was much tastier than the Atlantis Steak  Seafood restaurant's was.

<Author>ORPlatypus
<Content>super service We had read the reviews and decided that this hotel sounded just fine for a family group of four that would spend little time in a room. What we got was phenominal service, friendly people and a great room. Moments after our arrival we realized that we had left the small bag with the passports and all the money (cash) on the airport bus. The hotel desk instantly tracked down the bus company through their dispatcher and had the bus driver check and bring our bag to the hotel. The bus captian, bar staff and housekeepers answered all our stupid questions with smiles and gave us excellent answers that saved us money and time. Remembering that this is a humid and warm climate, so a little mold in a back corner did not bother us. The rooms had great air conditioning and lots of warm water in the showers. The Pali tower is the best view and actually a pool in the shade (only one at a time) worked out well for the one in our group who got burnt. In all, a great experience at a very economical price. We would recommend it to any of our friends.

<Author>Arrege
<Content>Decent Budget hotel and close to the beach My wife and I stayed at this hotel from March 15-22 2007. We are both in our 30s and this was our 4th time to Honolulu. We read several reviews of this hotel before booking it...which we did using a site called 'Pleasant Holidays'. The hotel price was the main attraction..since it was about $500 less than several nearby competitors.The Hotel is located 1 block from the beach and is closer to the Diamond Head side of Wiakiki. We got there around noon and the room was not ready till 3 pm, so we left our bags with security.Our first room had a queen bed and was on the 'Kuhio Street' side. It was clean, small and comfortable. The main problem was the noise. We could not sleep that first night since there was so much street noise. After complaining to the staff the next day, they moved us to the 'Ocean View' side...away from the street. This was better and we could get a good night rest.The rooms are not insulated from the outside weather/noise, so you can still hear loud noises from the street. If it is chilly outside, then you can feel the draft thru the sliding door.Our floor was quiet and fortunately, we had no noisy neighbors. The hotel is popular with people of all ages and it was very busy during our stay...so a lot of people do go to this hotel.Pros:Good PriceClose to the beachOcean View rooms DO have a view of the ocean :)there is an ABC store next doorFree Beach Towels (as many as you want)Management/Staff was helpful and responsiveCons:Rooms not insulated from outside noiseKuhio St. side rooms should be avoidedClose to Diamond Head side, so we had to walk 5 blocks to a sandier beach or to the food pantry on KuhioOverall, this is a decent budget hotel in a good location. If you want a classier/modern hotel then you should be prepared to pay more.

<Author>prettyangel687
<Content>Decent and OK I booked through pleasant holidays. It was a special and for two ppl it cost us $711, including taxes! Great deal, and we traveled 3/17-3/20. For a 2 star hotel i wasn't expecting too much. Especially after reading the mixed reviews on this website. We were hoping for a upgrade but we didnt recieve one. They were going to charge me $45 extra a night for a upgrade to a room with a kitchenette. Happy i didnt upgrade since our friends did. The kitchenette was a microwave and a hotplate. Yes the room was bigger, but the bathroom was actually dirtier then ours. Stains in the sink, ect, which our room did not have. They also only paid and extra $25 a night for their room, so if you are looking to upgrade, negotiate.  Our room was on the 7th floor with a tiny view of the ocean in between two buildings. The balcony was VERY small and narrow, enough to fit 2 chairs and thats about it. Room was clean, and decent. Bed was not that soft, but sleepable. They gave us 2 big towels to shower with and thats it. Dont know if you can get extra since we didnt need any extra. Bathroom was small, had a hair dryer and came with a shower and no tub. They did give soap and lotions, but no hair cap if that matters to you. No room service. The pool was on the 3rd floor and it consisted of two seperate SMALL pools. Like i said for a 2 star it was what i was expecting overall. All i really cared about was that it was clean and that is what i got. Location is actually very good. One semi-long block from the beach. I dont know what ppl are complaining about it being too far because it is NOT. The block is the size of maybe 1 1/2 - 2 blocks at most. Its near the strip so of course plenty of places to eat at. When i did talk to the staff they were nice, but i never really asked them for anything. They did have valet and they charged $15 a day which you dont pay directly to the hotel. You actually pay the valet which i think is ran by a company called ameripark?? Something along that line. They only had one person working at all times, and when they get your car it does take about 5-10 minutes. Longer if they just left to get someone else's car before you. The reason being i think is that when they get your car they have to drive around the block since the hotel is on a one way street. I heard there is a parking lot down the street or something that is only $8 a day. We were only staying for 3 days so i didnt bother. I just paid the premium.I've stayed at many hotels including luxury 5 star and i did not have any complaints about this 2 star hotel. I knew it was a 2 star when i booked and wasnt expecting anything fantastic. If you want a good location, clean, cheap place to sleep this would be it. I'm not sure what the regular rates are, but i dont think i would pay more then $100 a night for this place.

<Author>gmfibes
<Content>Just stayed 8 days at the Ocean Resort Spent 8 days at the OR. Booked a partial ocean view room, # 1004, directly by phone in advance, with a senior discount available to those over 55. Was upgraded at the desk when we arrived to room # 1204 in the older tower when I mentioned I had stayed at the hotel 2 years prior and had a great experience. Room was small but very clean with 1 queen bed. NO problems whatsoever: bathroom clean, carpets clean, NO mold, NO waterstains, NO bugs. View was fantastic from our balcony. Being given a room 2 floors higher than originally booked was definately a plus as the higher you go the better the view. NEVER waited for more than 15 seconds for an elevator as one was usually available within 10 seconds. OR is close to the beach, park, zoo, etc. Will definately stay there again. Book this hotel if you are on a budget, and want a clean room for a very good price. If you want a Hotel that is extravagant and has every bell and whistle, stay somewhere else for 2-5 times the price.

<Content>Great view -- rooms need help. We stayed 3 nights at the Ocean Resort Hotel in Wikiki from 2/18/07 - 2/21/07. We found the location great (other than being the last to be dropped off on the transfer from the airport). The view of Waikiki, only a block away was great from our ocean view room. The elevators were slow -- sometimes not even moving at all -- we walked down 11 floors when the one on our floor wouldn't move and the other wouldn't come. At check out time, we called the desk to tell them we were having the same problem again and couldn't manage to get our luggage down without the elevator. We weren't expecting the property to be top of the line -- the price was very reasonable -- but we were disappointed with what we got.

<Author>Travel_Girl00
<Content>Can't go wrong for the price We stayed here one night, before moving on to our timeshare in Ko'olina. If you want cheap and close to the beach, try this place but don't expect 5 star!

<Author>Toucanfran
<Content>Great for the Price This hotel was great for the price we paid. If you're into a simple clean place to stay with no frills, this is the place for you. Location is fantastic, close to beach, zoo, aquarium, TONs of shopping and ABC stores as well as restaurants. You can walk to almost everyting or take the FREE shuttle that stops outside the hotel. The room was clean with a bit of wear and tear to be expected. The valet told to us to park in the gargae across the street if we wanted to self park which saved us $7.00/day in parking. upon arrival, we opened the curtain to the balconey to discover a beautiful view of the ocean and Diamondhead. We were on the 9th floor (highest we could go for what we paid) in the Diamondhead Tower (older of the 2). Our door lock was broken and minifridge was in disrepair, but with a quick call, the helpful staff had it fixed in about an hour and we had a brand new fridge. I highly recommend this hotel for travelors who are looking for a clean, inexpensive practical place to stay with a great location.

<Author>Seajax
<Content>Waikiki on a budget I booked this hotel through Expedia on an excellent package deal, so I knew it wasn't going to be anything spectacular like the Four Seasons. The room was a bit humid, but then again, Hawaii in general is...turning on the A/C took care of that. However, the A/C was LOUD, and kept waking me up during the night. The room was dated, however as everything in Hawaii is much more than what you pay on the mainland, the price of staying at the Ocean Hotel can't be beat. Its only a couple minutes walk to the beach, Honolulu Zoo, shopping and ABC store. If you've never been to Hawaii before, you'll get a kick out of counting how many ABC stores you can count in one day! Also, you can catch the city bus on the corner which will take you further down the Waikiki strip to the Ala Moana Mall. I also rented a car one day, and was in walking distance of Hertz.If you do take tours in Hawaii, remember everything is Island Time...which means they will be about 20 minutes late picking you up. I panicked at first thinking they forgot us, but caught on after the second tour. This also means the housekeeping is very slow and late in the day also. Sometimes, they didn't show up until almost 5pm...and it would take them a loooong time to finish cleaning a room. In summary, stay here if you aren't too picky about your lodgings and want a great deal to stay. It may not be the nicest, and doesn't look the prettiest, but the location and price make up for it. Everything in Hawaii is expensive!! Food (even the grocery stores) will cost much more than what it does on the mainland, especially in Waikiki. To stay at the Ocean gives your wallet a bit of a break in a place that isn't cheap to travel to.  
<Date>Jan 4, 2007

<Author>YOSEgal
<Content>Try to get a high level floor The hotel was chosen for my husband and I as we were on a business trip and they paid all expenses. We were in an out and stayed 3 separate times as we also had to go to Lanai and Molokai. Each night we stayed in a different room. Two were on the 9th floor and one was on the 11th floor. All had views of the beach, although you still look over apartments and hotels. The room rate was $69/night which is very cheap in Waikiki. We were there about 1.5 weeks before the 6.6 earthquake hit, but the trade winds had stopped blowing and it was the most miserable week - hot, humid days and nights. We were glad for air conditioning in the room. The room was okay, with a small refrigerator in the room under the bathroom sink, but here are the shortcomings: very hard bed-felt the springs, no hair dryer in room and none available (you can rent from the gift shop, but none were available during my stay), no microwave, small counter space next to sink, no coffeemaker in room. It had a small lanai (porch) with two chairs. Too hot to enjoy though. The hotel restaurant did not look like it was worth going too - they had a menu with pictures outside the door. It kept me away!Postives: The toilet and large shower stall (no tub) were in a separate room, apart from the sink. The room had room darkening curtains to keep out the bright morning sun as well as keep the room cooler in the afternoon  evening. The air conditioner had digital controls for adjusting the temperature and fan speed. We could keep the fan blowing the entire time which helped to drown out street noise. The compressor kept coming on and off, but we got used to that. The hotel is about 2 blocks from the beach and at the end of the Waikiki area, but plenty of shops around to walk through next to the beach. There is an ABC store 1 block away, short blocks too. That is where we got coffee and breakfast items like yogurt and cereal/milk. One room we got to view only was on the 14th floor and it was nicer in that it had a hair dryer attached to the wall! But, we couldn't stay there and asked for another room since we got in after 9 p.m. and the a/c had not been on. The staff was gracious and gave us another room on the 11 th floor that the a/c had been on. But no hair dryer! I tried to be appreciative and not be ugly when I asked about another room and the hair dryers - so was treated very well by the staff. Overall, the room is okay if you don't mind hard beds, buy coffee outside the hotel, and having no microwave or hair dryer.The next week when on our vacation part of the trip, we stayed at the Aqua Palms at the other end of Waikiki. It was a huge improvement. I got that room for $125/night with my AAA discount. It had a great bed and a comfortable sofa (makes into a bed) with microwave, refrigerator, and coffeemaker and hairdryer. See my detailed review later for that hotel.

During my first stay in '96, the low room rates were very attractive and location great. Even at that time, the hotel was obviously dated and in need of a facelift but was tolerable. During my stay there last week, I realized the the facelift and renovations which could have helped 10 years ago are absolutely needed now. The place is a dump now ... it is drab, run down and moldy smelling.If you are on a tight budget, want a good location in Waikiki, and just a place to sleep and bathe, then stay at this property -- but don't pay more than $50 a night. The rack rates they charge at this hotel are outrageous for the poor quality of accommodations and lack of service.Funny thing is that whenever I stay here (summertime), the hotel is either close to capacity or completely full. They are one of the lower priced hotels in Waikiki, but why does the ownership not re-invest money in at least properly maintaining this property which is in a prime location?? it is sad to see the decline of this property and nothing visibly being done about it.Things I didn't like on my last stay: Old, sagging mattresses (bedsheets and pillow cases are clean, though). Mattresses showed terribly obvious dips on the side of the bed close to the telephone and were uncomfortable to sleep in when permanently dipped so badly. Large, dark stains in the carpet which weren't removed. Our bathroom had no fan or air circulation whatsoever. As a result, the wood frame door is peeling from the dampness due to lack of ventilation. Overall, just a drab, dirty feeling to not just my room but the property in general.Biggest gripe: Parking. I was told by one of the parking valet people that the hotel only has 80 parking spaces in its garage, and the hotel has 400 rooms. They directed me and other guests to park across the street (across busy Kuhio Avenue) at the Waikiki Banyan -- extremely inconvenient and also a very crowded parking structure of its own. Ocean Resort's parking valet attendants didn't even offer to valet park their guests cars at their overflow parking location at Wki Banyan. In hindsight, I would have paid to have an Ocean Resort valet guy park my car at this satellite location, but they didn't even offer it. Another example of their poor, poor service.I am very disappointed in the decline of this property, service-wise and also with the physical deterioration. In previous years, I would have highly recommended it to people for value of their money. But after last week's stay, I would not recommend at all. It is not worth one's money, in my opinion. With hotel rates generally high in Waikiki, your money is better spent elsewhere for better quality.  
<Date>Jul 7, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Disgusting Hotel We live on the westside of Oahu and decided to spend my daughter's sweet sixteen birthday which also fell on Memorial day weekend at a hotel in Waikiki. I found affordable rooms at the Ocean Resort Hotel, so we rented two deluxe with kitchenette rooms for two nights. My husband and I drove up in two different cars to the hotel entrance and was told to park around the corner which is where the hotel parking is located. It was a dark underground parking lot that was cramped and had no open parking stalls, there was actually more storage of table, chairs and dumpsters than parking stalls. We were then told to exit the parking structure and go around the city block and enter another parking entrance which was no cleaner or safer but it did have two stalls left which was a rip off for $10 a day per car parking fees. The hotel lobby was adequate and the staff was polite entering our rooms was shocking. The rugs were stained with food, drink and cigarette burns, there were live ant trails from the cabinets to the sink in the kitchen. The bath tub had live roaches and ants crawling every where and the bathroom sink leaked all day and night. The bathroom was so tiny you had to tuck in your legs on the toilet to shut the door. Our second hotel room had broken glass on the rug near the kitchen area from a microwave plate that must have been broken from the guest before us. The room was so gross we showered in the tub with our bathing suits on and we slept on sleeping bags on top of the bed covers. It was a disaster for my daughter, she was embarrassed for her best friend who spent the weekend with our family. We tried to spend as much time as we could out of the room so not to ruin our weekend. I will never go to that hotel ever again, it was literally a roach motel.

<Author>holjim
<Content>Cannot beat for the Price I've just returned from my first trip to Hawaii and wanted to throw in my two cents about the Ocean Resort Hotel in Waikiki. I booked my room very last minute and was a little nervous after reading some of the reviews of the hotel. I had visions of killer roaches and mysterious stains as I took the old but perfectly fine elevator up to the 12th floor.To my surprise and joy, there were no odors, bugs or unpleasant hotel staff.We had a clean room in an average hotel literally two blocks from the beach for $59.Granted, anyone can have a good or bad experience at a hotel and I'm not doubting that people have had a bad time there but in my case, everything was fine and I certainly enjoyed putting my saved money to better use in hawaii. If you think your $59 should get you the Surfrider or Outrigger experience, you probably shouldn't be reviewing hotels. However, if you want a clean room in a great location without much in the way of frills, I absolutely recommend the Ocean Resort.

<Content>value for money We stayed in room 840 with city/diamond head views and kitchenette. The room was very spacious, clean and well equipped. Not what you want after a 15 hour flight. Take a taxi for the few extra bucks. it's worth it.Ocean Resort is not 5 star, but is good value for money  the location can't be beat. Will definitely stay there again.

<Author>TParty
<Content>Perfectly Fine We just returned from spending nine nights at this hotel and found it to be just fine. We had a large room with two full beds and a divan/single bed. There was a small kitchenette with everything we needed. The room was clean, not spotless, and comfortable. The TV worked well and had good reception on all channels. We found the staff friendly enough, certainly not rude as a few posters have noted. Our room was always cleaned before noon. The air conditioning worked well. The paper was delivered to our door every morning except Sunday. We didn't use the pool, it didn't look that inviting. The coffeemaker was small and didn't make very good coffee, but we found the Honolulu Coffee Company in the lobby of the Moana Surfrider and that became our daily treat. Price and proximity to the beach are two of this hotel's greatest assets. The Bus is just across the street and remember to get a transfer, you can use it in either direction, the drivers were generous with the expiration time and we never had to pay for our trip back. Yes, the place was a little tatty, but even the most expensive, 4-5 star hotels on the beach had faded lobby carpeting in need of a good vacuum. This is a relaxed beach community and that is just how things are. I never saw one prostitute near this hotel, granted we were in by 9:30-10:00pm each night. I would recommend Wolfgang Pucks at the end of the road for good food at a good price. We had a good experience at the Ocean Beach and would stay there again, definitely.

<Author>planetrj
<Content>3 C's - Excellent Value Overall In Waikiki! Personally, I cannot understand why there are so many terrible reviews. This is my 4th trip to Oahu, and each time I have stayed here, I always try to find a place that is less expensive, because I realize how little time I really spend in the room. I guess, if you come all the way to Waikiki and just stay in the room, then this may not be the perfect place. I honestly don't come here to get room pampering, nor do I come for the room service. Comfort, Clean, and Convenient - THAT is exactly what I got!Accessibility: The hotel's geographic location is just about the best you can get. It's on Paoakalani St. that takes you 2 blocks to the beach (Kuhio Beach - very nice little beach), and the corner of Kuhio Ave, which takes you right to Duke's Lane, the market, and all the restaurants, clubs and shops too. Driving to Diamond Head is a breeze, as you only need to turn 1 corner to get to the street that takes you there.Room Comfort: The rooms are very oversized large, and have airy patios and balconies with big glass sliding doors, so that you can let in the good ol' ocean breeze in. Long and low dressers with lots of drawers to store clothing, etc. They come with good built-in A/C's, and work very efficiently (though I only needed to use mine the first day, till I was acclimated). The room I HIGHLY recommend is one with a kitchenette. They come completely equipped with a hot plate, dishes, silverwear, pots/pans, dish towels, and dishsoap! Even a stay at the expensive Ilikai didn't equip dishsoap.... Kudos! (who wants to pay $4 for a full bottle dishsoap when you'll probably use about 2 tbsp., anyways?). The kitchenette also comes with a newer microwave, sink, and small refrigerator - big enough to put in plenty of food storage. The kitchenette was VERY useful in helping save more money too, as you can supplement your dining out with breakfasts and lunches in the room, then splurge on a nice dinner out! Surely saved over $300+ (more I am sure) cooking my meals in-room. The beds were overly firm for my taste (standard hotel issue), but was easily resolved by requesting about 5 blankets. Housekeeping was quick and happy to ablige me with as many blankets as I needed. Make sure you request to stay in the Pali Tower, as this is the side with the cleanest halls/rooms.Front Desk: Nothing bad to say about front desk. Quick, efficient, and very friendly. Checkin took no more than 5 minutes. They were friendly enough to ask if I needed anything else after any request. Room keys are credit cards, so they are very convenient and easy to put into swimming trunks or shorts.Housekeeping: Even a couple days where I slept in late, I would put the 'clean room' sign out, and they would still clean the room at 11am, which was very nice. They do an excellent job of cleaning, and even refill soaps, shampoos, and tissues every day. Extra towels were no issue, and they would always bring extra until the day I left. They also cleaned up my dirty dishes and folded my clothes on the bed, which was very pleasing, and again, quite surprising, as this never happened at more expensive hotels.Nearby Restaurants/Shops: The location is VERY convenient for several staples for the average tourist. First, there is an ABC store downstairs on the sidestreet (like a 7-11 and tourist gift shop all-in-one). Open till midnight, makes for a great quickie run store. Then, down the street, there's a Seattle's Best Coffee shop, Italian Restaurant, Tiki's Restaurant (very good food and live music), and Cheeseburger In Paradise (AMAZING BURGERS!) about 4 blocks away. The restaurant inside the hotel in the main lobby was inexpensive, but just average dining (like Coco's or Denny's). They did offer Hawaiian Breakfast though, and Portugese Sausage and Eggs, which was pretty good (about $10/person for breakfast and drink).Parking Lot: There's a Diamond parking lot underneath the hotel that was incredibly easy to get to (entering by the elevator). Also, it was MUCH less expensive (at $10/day) than what I had paid for previously (normally costs about $16 - 20 per 24 hours depending on the hotel).I will be returning to Ocean Resort Hotel Next year, as I have found my 'perfect balance' of value between comfort and best price. Thanks Ocean Resort! :)  
<Date>May 20, 2006

<Content>Great place to stay We stayed at the Ocean Resort April 19-23. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Maybe it was just the warm weather - but we liked it a lot! After lots and lots of travelling around the States for two weeks, we arrived at Honolulu for a one night stay before our return to Australia. We had booked the Ocean Resort after lots of research, including TripAdvisor, and looking for a decent property at a decent (mid-range) price.We arrived at the hotel at 4.30pm - quick check-in and up to a room on the 10th floor. We booked and received a 'moderate ocean view' room, which was fairly small by US standards, but was very clean, and comfortable.There was a small balcony as reported by other posters here - just deep enough for two chairs. The room directly faced Waikiki Beach, and of the 100% potential view, I guess about 65% of the beach was obscured by surrounding buildings - but this still left us with a 35% uninterrupted view of the ocean and sunset - well above what we had expected! The room itself was basic, television, table, couple of inside chairs and bedside lamps, a small fridge. No tea and coffee making facilities - however you can buy a hot cup of coffee in the mornings from the hotel's restaurant for USD1.05 (hot and wet but not spectacular). Also an air-conditioner, small area for luggage (and the bathroom sink), then a small bathroom with shower and wc. Plenty of towels, and basic amenities of soap, shampoo/conditioner (mixed), and lotion.Staff were friendly and helpful - no problems with check-in or out. If you need a shuttle to the airport it can be arranged at the bell desk - but you need to pay in cash (USD9 per person), and reservations need to be made by 7.00pm. The shuttle itself was on time.One of the good things about the hotel was its location - it says it is one and a half blocks from the beach, but Waikiki is very small, and the walk itself is about 3 minutes, with lots of food outlets and restaurants nearby.Would stay again, and it was the perfect place for a single night or couple of nights, although we have no other experience of hotels in the area so it is a little difficult to compare, except that the larger hotels have price tags to match!

<Content>Avoid this place I am usually not very demanding about hotels in Waikiki 鈥?it鈥檚 just a place to sleep for me. I don鈥檛 need plush robes or fancy amenities. Also, I grant you that I was here during the storm of 2006, so it was a depressing time to be in Hawaii. But this hotel made all of that WORSE. I agree, budget hotels are basic but budget should not mean shabby, sloppy upkeep and perfunctory staff. But that鈥檚 what I found here. I got the impression that nobody was in charge, nobody was supervising the staff or the physical condition of the hotel, and nobody cared about the kind of impression the hotel conveyed.First: the attitude of the staff was bordering on rude. While I was checking in, a man asked the other desk clerk where the bellman is, since he needed to get his bags. The desk clerk says, 鈥渙h, he鈥檚 around, he鈥檒l be back.鈥?He didn鈥檛 offer to find the bellman, or offer any help to the guy to retrieve the bags. On another day, a different desk clerk was asked if a particular hotel employee was on duty. The clerk replied, 鈥淥h, I don鈥檛 know, you could call his office.鈥?She sounded as if she鈥檇 never heard of this staff person and she made no effort to find out if he was around. Just, 鈥測ou can call his office.鈥?Both of these people might as well have come straight out and said, 鈥渄on鈥檛 bother me.鈥?Second: it鈥檚 physically shabby. On my floor (12th) the wallpaper on the decorative panel opposite the elevator had been torn off in strips, with bare plaster on part of it and strips of wallpaper hanging on part of it. It remained in that condition for the entire ten days I stayed there 鈥?apparently no one could be bothered to fix it. Third: the hotel was being painted. Not usually a big deal to me, hotels have to be painted and you can鈥檛 shut them while that happens. But somebody should have checked up on these painters. When they painted the elevator frames they put the wet paint signs INSIDE the elevator, on top of the ad for the lobby shop. Obviously, this had not been painted, and there were no wet paint signs on the elevator frames-- which had been painted. I found this out when I held the elevator door open for another guest and got blue paint all over my hands. Not a major problem, I grant you, but it all denotes laziness and lack of attention. Fourth: I stayed in the Pali Tower which had only two elevators, and no service elevator, so there were frequently long waits for the elevator. Since the service staff had to use the guest elevators this increased the delays and also meant that guests got to share the elevator with large rolling hampers of dirty laundry and, sometimes, trash bags. Fifth: someone needs to work on the pool area. It鈥檚 ugly. The green outdoor carpet is worn, there was trash on the carpeting, and paint was visibly chipping on the concrete walls of the pool deck. No effort was made to keep it tidy, let alone nice. The location is good, near the beach, and the cleaning staff were courteous 鈥?maybe they should promote them to the front desk 鈥?and took good care of my room. My room itself was fine for a budget hotel.I've stayed in Waikiki budget hotels before, so I know what to expect from a budget hotel as opposed to a luxury hotel. But in all those other places, the staff was courteous and helpful and had a pleasant attitude. This place rubbed in the fact that you were staying in an inexpensive hotel, as if it鈥檚 OK to be rude and let the hotel run down since the people who stay there don鈥檛 have a lot of money. I have NEVER run into that kind of attitude or shabbiness before. I will never go back to this place.

<Author>SOULjourner
<Content>Great Value and Location My husband and I stayed at the Ocean Resort Hotel Waikiki for six nights (March 24-30) after booking a reservation through Great Hawaii Vacations ($506 for a standard Diamond Tower room with queen bed, including tax). We were upgraded to an ocean view room with a small lanai (just deep enough for a couple of chairs) on the seventh floor. Even though the furnishings and d茅cor are dated, the room was clean, comfortable and in good working order. We had all the basic necessities鈥攁ir conditioning, TV, phone (they do charge 75 cents for local calls and a dollar for 800 access), clock/radio, a small refrigerator in the bathroom, and hot water with good pressure anytime we needed it. A safe is available (we didn鈥檛 use it; I believe there may be an extra charge for that). On the third floor, there are two pools and a sundeck as well as an ice machine and a dispenser for instant hot water (which we used to make tea, oatmeal, and cup-a-noodles). There is a coin op laundry on the second floor. (A hair dryer and coffee maker in the room would have been nice additions.)  Downstairs, there is internet access for 15 cents a minute, booking agents for activities, two gift shops, the Punawai Lounge (open at 4 pm with well drinks for $4), and a mediocre caf茅 (not recommended; also, they automatically add a 15% service charge to your tab). The desk will fax documents for you at $1 per page. Parking is available at $10 per day, but you really don鈥檛 need a car because the hotel鈥檚 location is so convenient鈥攁bout a block and a half to the beach and steps to several bus lines, including the #2 and #13 on Kuhio and the Kapahulu lines. The trolley for Ala Moana Center stops right in front of the hotel. Easy walking distance to the zoo (enjoyable and cheap at $6 for adults, nice snack station), Kapiolani Park, Waikiki Aquarium, shopping, and eateries (Starbucks is about two blocks away on the corner of Kapahulu and Kalakaua, across from the park), as well as some of the pricier hotels. A new ABC store just opened a half-block toward the beach, so you can pop in for bottled water, snacks (musubi, fruit, ice cream, sandwiches), wine, beach mats, bus passes or whatever. We would definitely stay at the Ocean Resort Hotel Waikiki again.

<Author>Janet McPherson
<Content>same old same old Have been returning to this hotel since 1997 and the price has risen considerably over that period, but it is difficult to see any money being spent on the property. Bedspreads, carpets, fridge and fitted furniture could all do with a facelift and new elevators are long overdue. Bathroom could also do with some attention and a coat of paint would not come amiss. <Author>Vacation Val
<Content>Good value hotel My husband and I just got back from Waikiki. Stayed 1 week at the Ocean Resort. No complaints. After reading all the negative reviews, we were very skeptical but we have to say that we were pleasantly surprised. Yes, it could use a facelift but for the price we paid we're not about to complain about esthetics. The staff was friendly. The room was clean - no bugs. It had a small table with 2 chairs, dresser, t.v., dresser, comfy bed with good pillows and the toilet / shower were separate from the sink. Yes they should spring for a new soap dish in the shower but a rusty soap dish and a bad caulking job in the shower didn't deter us. There was always hot water and lots of soft towels. (We've been in 4* hotels where the towels were so rough they could take your skin off!) The maid usually didn't get there until after 3 each day but made a point of telling us that she was not ignoring our clean room sign but said she had orders to clean the check out rooms first so new people could check in by 3. Nevertheless she was always there with a smile and a thank you for the tip we always left. We had a fair sized balcony with 2 chairs so we could enjoy happy hour on our own lanai while enjoying the warm weather while watching the tourists go by. The only real disappointment was the pool deck. The lounge chairs were in a sad state - most had hardly any webbing left on them. You had to watch how you sat down. They pool deck itself was done in green artifical turf which certainly could use upgrading. We ate in the hotel restaurant a couple of times and found the food quite tasty and very reasonably priced. It seemed to be full all the time. They also have a lounge that offers drink specials each day. Unbelievable but more times than not, there was an elevator waiting in the lobby to take us up to our room. We didn't find we were ever waiting for an elevator (contrary to some reviews). Overall, I would recommend this hotel for travellers looking for a good priced hotel close to the beach and other amenities. The Ritz it ain't - but clean, affordable and in an excellent location it is!  
<Date>Mar 3, 2006

<Author>SPUDISLANDER1
<Content>Great Stay at Ocean Resort My wife and I just got back from 8 days in Waikiki at the Ocean Resort. We had a room on the 2nd floor overlooking the back alley and thoroughly enjoyed it.The hotel was clean and the staff very friendly. Always a smile at the front desk when we went in.The room although rather plain had a very comfortable king size bed and was very quiet.  Location was great because it was within walking distance of everything we wanted to do. We rented a car for 3 days and did not have to drive through the city in order to get to the highway. We found this great. The hotel is directly across the street from the Marriott on the Beach which is very convenient because all of the tour buses leave from there.The Marriott also has a coffee shop which we frequented in the morning and an ABC store which was open till midnight. Since we were on the 2nd floor we could either walk up to our room or take one of the three elevators. The laundry room was down the hall from us and this was very convenient. The day we left we booked out at 12:00 however we were not being picked up for the airport until 10:30 PM since our flight was not leaving until 1:30 AM (Air Canada). The hotel staff made sure that we were comfortable the rest of the day and looked after us until the shuttle arrived. I would highly recommend this hotel to anyone and thank you Ocean Resort staff for making 2 Canadians first trip to Hawaii a very enjoyable and memorable one.

<Author>tuffysoftballmom
<Content>LOCATION! LOCATION! LOCATION! I stayed with my 3 children and my mom in this hotel during the last week of January. While the public areas were noticably worn, the room and furnishings (although older)were clean and well-maintained. We had a kitchenette which had a small refrigerator, microwave, coffeemaker and cooktop. Bring your own coffee, as the hotel does not provide any. My room also had an iron and ironing board (room 1133)although, if you call and ask, the desk will tell you rooms do not have irons.Parking is 10.00 per day and you must pay daily and pay cash to the attendant. The parking is only for OceanResort guests, but is very limited and worth the 10.00 as it allows you to come and go as you please without the hassle of trying to locate a parking place.The great selling point of this hotel is the location. Located in almost the middle of Waikiki, we were several blocks from the Oceanarium Restuarant, International Market, Zoo, Aquarium, and two blocks from the beach. This made it very easy to walk EVERYWHERE which is great, since there is no public parking anywhere close.I found the hotel staff to be very friendly and most helpful in all aspects of tourist care. The tour guide in the lobby was also great and didn't mind answering questions even though I never purchased a tour from him.I noticed several of these reviews talked about the slow elevators. Between 3:00 PM and about 5:30 PM, the tour buses check in and it is a long wait for the elevators, however, this is understandable, and any other time the wait was reasonable.All in all, if you are looking for a 5 star hotel, this is definitely NOT it, but if you want a clean family-oriented hotel for a great price, this is the place.Just a tourist note: We went to Atlantis Submarine Tours and were VERY disappointed. It was 275.00 for 5 people and we thought we would see more fish and marine life than we did. Maybe it was just a slow fish day, but it is worth mentioning. Also, LOVED Germaines Laoua (bad spelling) ALOHA!!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Stay at the Ocean Resort We just got back from 5 days at the Ocean Resort. We had a great time. The room was nothing fancy, but it was better than I expected. We had a Deluxe Ocean view wit the kitchenette. It was as described. We had a pretty good view of Waikiki Beach. The room was clean. No bugs or anything. We were on the 11th floor. We saved a lot of money by having lunch in the room. I had no problem getting in the parking lot every day. It is a small lot, but I always had a space and they will hold one for you if you pay for it everyday. For $118.00 per night, it's one of the best values on Waikiki w/kitchenette. Sounds like people are not enjoying the cheaper rooms. After 5 days there, we spent 5 days at the Turtle Bay Resort. There is no comparison, but I did not expect there to be. Both hotels were exactly what I needed. I would stay at the Ocean Resort again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I would stay here again I stayed here for five nights. I booked the hotel thru Expedia and paid about $82 per night plus taxes for a standard no-view room and I was pleasantly surprised. I wasn't expecting much and maybe that's why. The room is a nice size for 1-2 people. It was clean and the staff was very friendly, although they are a little understaffed.The hotel itself is in a good location, about a 7 minute walk to the beach. Plenty of restaurants are a block or two away and a Starbucks about 3 blocks away. Also, they have wifi access in the lobby. However, my room was on the second floor and I was actually able to log on to my computer and connect from my room which is very nice for those who care about those things. Beds are standard for this category of hotel. Not the most comfortable, but it'll do. Bathroom was small. My only real complaint was that my room looked out onto a parking lot and a ramshackle building across the way. So if you want a view of any sort, you should definitely pay extra for it. For the money, the location, nice staff and a clean hotel, I would definitely stay again. Just don't expect luxury if you book. It's a standard hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good hotel for the frequent budget traveller I was a little skeptical of this 'budget' hotel at first but I took a chance. I booked online so it was even cheaper! I stayed at the Ocean Resort for 10 days and the service and the room was wonderful. If you plan on staying in your room most of the time then room service might be a problem. I was gone most of the time, so as long as the room was clean before i got back at night then it was fine. The staff were all courteous and very helpful and most of the hotels in Hawaii have there own tour guide or info center right in the hotel, for your convenience. The view wasn't that great but if you want a great view of the beach then why not just go to the beach!? I felt very safe in the hotel, left my passport, valuables and money without any problems. All in all, this was a great hotel for the money!

<Author>silverjym
<Content>Totally unimpressive I had booked a two week stay here in September in a Deluxe Ocean Front kitchenette for $99/night. Based on generally positive reviews, I was very disappointed in this hotel. This very drab room was good sized, clean but extremely worn with threadbare curtains and carpet, minimal banged up furniture and everything very worn in bathroom. Toilet seat was broken. Bath towels were thin and rough. Bath amenities were a bar of soap and shampoo/conditioner. Lanai had one chair (for a double room). Kitchenette had cube refrigerator, microwave and sink, one plate, two glasses, two mis-matched cups and four forks. Deluxe Ocean Front here means view of two somewhat distant slivers of ocean between other large buildings that are between this hotel and ocean. For a hotel to advertise ocean front one should receive a reasonable view of the ocean.The parking is a huge issue. When I checked in nobody mentioned prepaid parking reservations so when I returned in the evening there were no spaces available. The Waikiki Banyan across the street ($8.00) had a convention so no spaces available and there is no street parking. Ocean Resort's valet told me I could park in the zoo's parking lot several blocks away. He said night time parking was free. Wrong! I received a parking ticket for $35.00.I disagree with those who consider the neighborhood safe. Walking back from the zoo parking lot at 8:30 in the evening I was accosted by someone trying to sell me marijuana. I mentioned this to the valet and he said in a couple of hours the hookers would be out to join the marijuana sellers. Morning traffic is extremely noisy in Waikiki with delivery trucks and tour buses jockeying for space. Delivery trucks arrive as early as 5:00 a.m. Ocean Resort is on Paoakalani Avenue which is a major truck delivery route and bus pick up for tours. Truck and bus drivers are constantly honking at each other to try to get access into this narrow street and into hotel driveways. Because this area has such a density of high rise hotels the sound just amplifies and goes straight up. If you have issues with street noise, this is not the hotel for you. Based on the poor condition of the room, the extremely limited parking and the morning noise, I checked out and went to the Prince Kuhio which for less money provided a lovely, well cared for, sound proof room with plenty of parking. Also, staff there seemed happy to have my business--they thanked me for staying with them!Check in and check out at the Ocean Resort was fast with polite but totally uninterested staff. When I checked out the next morning there was no quiry why I was leaving 13 days early--perhaps the front desk is very accustomed to customers leaving after only one night?

<Author>netty_in_uk
<Content>Good base for exploring We stayed at the Ocean Resort as part of a longer trip/tour which included other destinations so we didn't actually choose this hotel, it came as part of the package.Firstly the location is great, a 2 minute walk to the beach/main touristy road through Waikiki. We stayed for 7 nights and found the hotel to be a good base for exploring. We had a deluxe kitchenette room without sea view. The room was quite large and reasonably comfortable although it was a little tatty. The rooms and communial areas are really just in need of a coat of paint and new carpets.We had 2 breakfasts in the restaurant which were ok and 1 evening meal which was poor - there are plenty of much better places to eat in Waikiki.We didn't use the pool as the hotel was so close to the beach but it is very small.Generally found the hotel staff a little unfriendly/unhelpful except the maid who was friendly and the man in the gift shop next to the lifts who was incredibly rude!To sum up I'd say this is a reasonable hotel, not the best I've stayed in by a long way but certainly not the worst (although it was the lowest standard of the hotels on our trip). Most people don't go to Hawaii to sit in their hotel room so if you're looking for a cheap base for exploring the Ocean Resort is fine. But if you're looking for luxury or something for a special occasion you may need to pay a little more and stay elsewhere.

<Author>Midnite13
<Content>Ocean View Deluxe - A Must I was a little worried about all the bad reviews I read. This hotel was great. The staff was courteous and professional at all times. Our room was on the 17th floor in Pali Tower overlooking Waikiki. While it didn't have the two beds I requested, I wasn't going to compromise the view. It took a minute to walk to the beach and even less to get to the Tiki Bar  Grill for nightly entertainment. We rented a car and found the valet service to be quick and efficient. Sundries and snacks could be purchased from any of the ABC convenience stores found on each block of Waikiki.The lot was full the first night we arrived but the staff directed us across the street for the same $10 after that they had room for our car. Enjoyed sitting on the balcony in the evening and watching the sunset and surfers. We used the concierge service to book a few tours - I was very disappointed with the daily tour of the Polynesian Cultural Center but loved the 7:30 evening show. If you can find it on your own, take the rent-a-car and avoid the touristy shows during the day. Went to a couple Luau's on the island and toured the coast. Don't swim in the lagoon part of Waikiki (with the breakwater), while it isn't as wavy, it's a virtual cesspool of trash and cigarette butts.I would definitely return to this hotel and would actually ask for the same room which included a table with 3 chairs and a kitchenette with mini fridge.

Our rooms didn't stink or have bugs, the paint wasn't peeeling and the elevators weren't slow, the staff was very friendly and the views from the rooms were great. Also the breakfasts were great at their restaraunt. The swamp coolers worked great. The location of the hotel is perfect. Just a 5-10 minute walk to Dukes. I don't know what people expect, but for $100 a night. This is the best I've seen.The valet is $10 for a 24 hour period(You need to rent a car). So you can come and go as you like and it's only $10. I felt this was ok. It doesn't take long at all to bring your car around. They have a guy to handle any activities you may want to do. They also have a small bar with very inexpensive drinks. I never went to the pool, but I walked by it. It's on the third floor and it's rather small. But it would be good for a dip after coming back from the beach.I would suggest snorkeling at Sharks Cove which is on the north shore. It's better than Hanauma Bay and less crowded. If you go to Hanauma Bay, go early, before 8:00AM. You will have to wait in line to get in after 8:00AM. You have to watch a 15 minute video and the line starts backing up. The blow hole is cool. Sunse Beach on the north shore is a great beach for the family and not crowded at all. Also don't miss the Dole Plantation. It's worth the stop. Pearl Harbor is neat, but kind of expensive. It's still a must do, but I really didn't enjoy it very much. Another fun event is renting an outrigger and riding 3 waves for $10 dollars. But you have to do the paddling. Also taking surf lessons is really fun if you've never done it before. Other than that, go to Dukes and have some drinks. The view is great. The Mai Tai Bar at the Royal Hawaiian is great as well. Take a Sunset Booze Cruise for $25. It was worth it as well.I highly recommend the Ocean Resort Hotel for those on a budget. Stay in a moderate oceanview room for the best view, but the smallest accomodations. Or you can stay in a Superior Kitchenette for a large room with a not so great view. But all the rooms have great balconies.  
<Date>Sep 6, 2005
